<p><b>Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport</b> (French: <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><i>Aéroport de Paris-Charles-de-Gaulle</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>CDG</b>, <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LFPG</b>), also known as <b>Roissy Airport</b> (name of the local district), is the largest <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in France. It is named after <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> (1890–1970), leader of the <a href="/wiki/Free_France" title="Free France">Free French Forces</a> during the Second World War, founder of the <a href="/wiki/French_Fifth_Republic" title="French Fifth Republic">French Fifth Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">President of France</a> from 1959 to 1969. Charles de Gaulle Airport is located within portions of several <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">communes</a> 25 km (16 mi)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIP_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-2">[2]</a></sup> to the northeast of <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. The airport serves as the principal <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> as well as a European hub for fellow <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> alliance partner <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>.</p>
<p>In 2015, the airport handled 65,766,986 passengers and 497,763 aircraft movements,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pax_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-pax-4">[4]</a></sup> thus making it the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">world's eighth-busiest airport</a> and Europe's second-busiest airport (after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow</a>) in terms of passenger numbers. It is also the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_traffic_movements" title="World's busiest airports by traffic movements">world's tenth-busiest</a> and it is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="Busiest airports in Europe">Europe's second-busiest airport</a> (after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow</a>) in aircraft movements. In terms of cargo traffic, the airport is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_cargo_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by cargo traffic">twelfth-busiest in the world</a> and the second-busiest in Europe (after <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>), handling 2,150,950 metric tonnes of cargo in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pax_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-pax-4">[4]</a></sup> The incumbent director of the airport, <a href="/wiki/Franck_Goldnadel" title="Franck Goldnadel">Franck Goldnadel</a>, was appointed to his position on 1 March 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport covers 32.38 square kilometres (12.50 sq mi) of land. The airport area, including terminals and runways, spans over three <i><a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">départements</a></i> and six <i><a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">communes</a></i>:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seine-et-Marne" title="Seine-et-Marne">Seine-et-Marne</a> <i>département</i>: <a href="/wiki/Le_Mesnil-Amelot" title="Le Mesnil-Amelot">Le Mesnil-Amelot</a> (Terminals 2E, 2F), <a href="/wiki/Mauregard" title="Mauregard">Mauregard</a> (Terminals 1, 3), and <a href="/wiki/Mitry-Mory" title="Mitry-Mory">Mitry-Mory</a> <i>communes</i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BEArep_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-BEArep-7">[7]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seine-Saint-Denis" title="Seine-Saint-Denis">Seine-Saint-Denis</a> <i>département</i>: <a href="/wiki/Tremblay-en-France" title="Tremblay-en-France">Tremblay-en-France</a> (Terminals 2A, 2B, 2C, 2D and Roissypôle) <i>commune</i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BEArep_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-BEArep-7">[7]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Val-d%27Oise" title="Val-d'Oise">Val-d'Oise</a> <i>département</i>: <a href="/wiki/Roissy-en-France" title="Roissy-en-France">Roissy-en-France</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89piais-l%C3%A8s-Louvres" title="Épiais-lès-Louvres">Épiais-lès-Louvres</a> <i>communes</i>.</li>
</ul>
<p>The choice of constructing an international aviation hub outside of central Paris was made due to a limited prospect of potential relocations or expropriations and the possibility of further expanding the airport in the future.</p>
<p>Management of the airport lies solely on the authority of <i><a href="/wiki/Paris_A%C3%A9roport" title="Paris Aéroport">Paris Aéroport</a></i>, which also manages <a href="/wiki/Orly_Airport" title="Orly Airport">Orly</a> (south of Paris), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris_%E2%80%93_Le_Bourget_Airport" title="Paris – Le Bourget Airport">Le Bourget</a> (to the immediate southwest of Charles de Gaulle Airport, now used for general aviation and Paris Air Shows), <a href="/wiki/Marsa_Alam_International_Airport" title="Marsa Alam International Airport">Marsa Alam</a> in Egypt, and several smaller airfields in the suburbs of Paris.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The planning and construction phase of what was known then as <i>Aéroport de Paris Nord</i> (Paris North Airport) began in 1966. On 8 March 1974 the airport, renamed Charles de Gaulle Airport, opened. Terminal 1 was built in an <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> design of a ten-floors-high circular building surrounded by seven satellite buildings, each with six gates allowing sunlight to enter through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apertures" title="Apertures">apertures</a>. The main architect was <a href="/wiki/Paul_Andreu" title="Paul Andreu">Paul Andreu</a>, who was also in charge of the extensions during the following decades.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_identity">Corporate identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Corporate identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Frutiger_(typeface)" title="Frutiger (typeface)">Frutiger typeface</a> was commissioned for use in the airport and implemented on signs throughout the building in 1975. Initially called <i>Roissy</i>, it was renamed after its designer <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Frutiger" title="Adrian Frutiger">Adrian Frutiger</a>.</p>
<p>Until 2005, every <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_address" title="Public address">PA announcement</a> made at Terminal 1 was preceded by a distinctive chime, nicknamed "Indicatif Roissy" and composed by <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Parmegiani" title="Bernard Parmegiani">Bernard Parmegiani</a> in 1971. The chime can be heard in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Polanski" title="Roman Polanski">Roman Polanski</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Frantic_(film)" title="Frantic (film)">Frantic</a></i>. The chime was officially replaced by the "Indicatif ADP" chime.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="680" data-file-width="1024" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg/220px-Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg/330px-Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg/440px-Terminal_1_of_CDG_Airport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CDG-aerialview.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/CDG-aerialview.jpg/220px-CDG-aerialview.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/CDG-aerialview.jpg/330px-CDG-aerialview.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/CDG-aerialview.jpg/440px-CDG-aerialview.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CDG-aerialview.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of Terminal 2A and 2B</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Charles de Gaulle Airport has three terminals: Terminal 1 is the oldest and situated opposite to Terminal 3; Terminal 2 is located at another side with 7 sub-terminal buildings (2A to 2G). Terminal 2 was originally built exclusively for <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>; since then it has been expanded significantly and now also hosts other airlines. Terminals 2A to 2F are interconnected by elevated and situated next to each other. Terminal 2G is a satellite building connected by shuttle bus.</p>
<p>Terminal 3 (formerly known as "Terminal 9") hosts charter and low-cost airlines. The <a href="/wiki/CDGVAL" title="CDGVAL">CDGVAL</a> light-rail shuttle connects Terminal 2 to Terminals 1/3 and their parking lots. Refer to <b>Ground Transportation</b> below for inter-terminal transfers and transport to central Paris.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first terminal, designed by Paul Andreu, was built in the image of an octopus. It consists of a circular terminal building which houses key functions such as check-in counters and baggage claim conveyors. Seven satellites with boarding gates are connected to the central building by underground walkways.</p>
<p>The central building, with a large skylight in its centre, dedicates each floor to a single function. The first floor is reserved for technical operations and not accessible to the public. The second floor contains shops and restaurants, the CDGVAL inter-terminal shuttle train platforms (for Terminal 2 and trains to central Paris) and check-in counters from a recent renovation. The majority of check-in counters, however, are located on the third floor, which also has access to taxi stands, bus stops and special pick-up vehicles. Departing passengers with valid boarding passes can reach the fourth floor, which houses duty-free stores and border control posts, for the boarding gates. The fifth floor contains baggage claim conveyors for arriving passengers. All four upper floors have assigned areas for parking and airline offices.</p>
<p>Passages between the third, fourth and fifth floors are provided by a tangle of escalators arranged through the centre of the building. These escalators are suspended over the central court. Each escalator is covered with a transparent tube to shelter from all weather conditions. These escalators were often used in film shootings (e.g. <i>The Last Gang of Ariel Zeitoun</i>). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alan_Parsons_Project" title="Alan Parsons Project">Alan Parsons Project</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/I_Robot_(album)" title="I Robot (album)">I Robot</a></i> features these escalators on its cover.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Terminal 2 is spread across seven sub-terminals: 2A to 2G. Terminals 2A to 2F are connected by inter-terminal walkways, but Terminal 2G is a satellite building 800 m (0.5 mi) away. Terminal 2G can only be accessed by shuttle bus from Terminals 1, 2A to 2F and 3. The CDGVAL inter-terminal shuttle train, Paris RER Regional-Express and high-speed TGV rail station, <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_2_TGV" title="Aéroport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV">Aéroport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV</a>, is located within the Terminal 2 complex and between 2C and 2E (on one side) or 2D and 2F (on the opposite side).</p>
<p>Terminal 2F was used for the filming of the music video for the <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Day" title="Beautiful Day">Beautiful Day</a>". The band also had their picture taken inside Terminal 2F for the album artwork of their 2000 album "<a href="/wiki/All_That_You_Can%27t_Leave_Behind" title="All That You Can't Leave Behind">All That You Can't Leave Behind</a>".</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Collapse_of_Terminal_2E">Collapse of Terminal 2E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Collapse of Terminal 2E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="389" data-file-width="485" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png/220px-Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png/330px-Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png/440px-Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Terminal_2E_CDG_collapse.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Collapsed Terminal 2E, June 2004</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CDG_Terminal_2.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="572" data-file-width="1380" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CDG_Terminal_2.png/220px-CDG_Terminal_2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CDG_Terminal_2.png/330px-CDG_Terminal_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CDG_Terminal_2.png/440px-CDG_Terminal_2.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CDG_Terminal_2.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Terminal 2</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 23 May 2004, shortly after the inauguration of terminal 2E, a portion of it collapsed near <a href="/wiki/Gate_(airport)" title="Gate (airport)">Gate</a> E50, killing four people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Two of the dead were reported to be Chinese citizens and another a Czech. Three other people were injured in the collapse. Terminal 2E had been inaugurated in 2003 after some delays in construction and was designed by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Andreu" title="Paul Andreu">Paul Andreu</a>. Administrative and judicial enquiries were started. Andreu also designed Terminal 3 at <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai International Airport</a>, which collapsed while under construction on 28 September 2004.</p>
<p>Before this accident, ADP had been planning for an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> in 2005 with the new terminal as a major attraction for investors. The partial collapse and indefinite closing of the terminal just before the beginning of summer seriously hurt the airport's business plan.</p>
<p>In February 2005, the results from the administrative inquiry were published. The experts pointed out that there was no single fault, but rather a number of causes for the collapse, in a design that had little margin for safety. The inquiry found the concrete <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">vaulted roof</a> was not resilient enough and had been pierced by metallic pillars and some openings weakened the structure. Sources close to the inquiry also disclosed that the whole building chain had worked as close to the limits as possible, so as to reduce costs. Paul Andreu denounced the building companies for having not correctly prepared the <a href="/wiki/Reinforced_concrete" title="Reinforced concrete">reinforced concrete</a>.</p>
<p>On 17 March 2005, ADP decided to tear down and rebuild the whole part of Terminal 2E (the "jetty") of which a section had collapsed, at a cost of approximately €100 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The reconstruction replaced the innovative concrete tube style of the jetty with a more traditional steel and glass structure. During reconstruction, two temporary departure lounges were constructed in the vicinity of the terminal that replicated the capacity of 2E before the collapse. The terminal reopened completely on 30 March 2008.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2G">Terminal 2G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Terminal 2G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg/220px-Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg/330px-Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg/440px-Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Display_Screen_At_A_Paris_Airport.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Terminal 2, display screen</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avions_2F.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="1023" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Avions_2F.jpg/220px-Avions_2F.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Avions_2F.jpg/330px-Avions_2F.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Avions_2F.jpg/440px-Avions_2F.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avions_2F.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> aircraft on stands at Terminal 2F at Charles de Gaulle Airport.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Push_Back_KLM.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="858" data-file-width="1278" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Push_Back_KLM.jpg/220px-Push_Back_KLM.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Push_Back_KLM.jpg/330px-Push_Back_KLM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Push_Back_KLM.jpg/440px-Push_Back_KLM.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Push_Back_KLM.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-700</a> push-back at Charles de Gaulle Airport.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Terminal 2G, dedicated to regional Air France flights and its affiliates, opened in 2008. This terminal is to the east of all terminals and can only be reached by shuttle bus. Terminal 2G is used for passengers flying in the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> (and thus has no passport control) and handles Air France regional and European traffic and provides small-capacity planes (up to 150 passengers) with a faster turnaround time than is currently possible by enabling them to park close to the new terminal building and boarding passengers primarily by bus, or walking. A bus line called "navette orange" connects the terminal 2G inside the safety check area with terminals 2E and 2F. Passengers transferring to other terminals need to take a bus in the public area, and therefore pass through safety checks again.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hall_L_.28Satellite_3.29">Hall L (Satellite 3)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hall L (Satellite 3)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The completion of 750 m (2,460 ft) long Satellite 3 (or S3) to the immediate east of Terminals 2E and 2F provides further <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jetways</a> for large-capacity airliners, specifically the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>. Check-in and <a href="/wiki/Baggage_handling_system" title="Baggage handling system">baggage handling</a> are provided by the existing infrastructure in Terminals 2E and 2F. Satellite 3 was opened in part on 27 June 2007 and fully operational in September 2007. It corresponds now to gates L of terminal 2E.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hall_M_.28Satellite_4.29">Hall M (Satellite 4)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hall M (Satellite 4)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The satellite S4, adjacent to the S3 and part of terminal 2E, officially opened on 28 June 2012. It corresponds now to gates M of terminal 2E. Dedicated to long-haul flights, it has the ability to handle 16 aircraft at the same time, with an expected capacity of 7.8 million passengers per year. Its opening has led to the relocation of all Skyteam airlines to terminals 2E (for international carriers), 2F (for Schengen European carriers) and 2G.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Air France has moved all of its operations previously located at 2C to 2E. In October 2012, 2F closed its international operations and became completely Schengen, allowing for all Air France flights currently operating in 2D to relocate to terminal 2F. Further, in April 2013, Terminal 2B closed for a complete renovation (all airlines relocated to 2D) and will receive upgrades including the addition of a second floor completely dedicated to arrivals. Once 2B is completed, 2D will close and receive similar upgrades, including the addition of a new floor. Low-cost carrier easyJet has shown its interest in being the sole carrier at 2B.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S4_ADP_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-S4_ADP-10">[10]</a></sup> To facilitate connections, a new boarding area between 2A and 2C was opened in March 2012. It allows for all security and passport control to be handled in a single area, allows for many new shopping opportunities as well as new airline lounges, and eases transfer restrictions between 2A and 2C.</p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/La_Tribune" title="La Tribune">La Tribune</a> newspaper a new Terminal 4 is likely to be built around 2025, when Charles de Gaulle Airport's maximum capacity of 80 millions will be reached. This new Terminal 4, when constructed, will be able to accommodate 30-40 million passengers per year and will most likely be built north of Terminal 2E.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_3">Terminal 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Terminal 3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Terminal 3 is located 1 km (0.62 mi) away from Terminal 1. It consists of separate buildings for arrivals and departures. The walking distance between Terminals 1 and 3 is 3 km (1.9 mi) long, however, the rail station (named as "CDG Airport Terminal 1") for RER and CDGVAL trains are only at a distance of 300 m (980 ft). Terminal 3 has no boarding gates constructed and all passengers are ferried via boarding buses to the aircraft stands.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Roissyp.C3.B4le">Roissypôle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Roissypôle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Roissypôle is a complex consisting of office buildings, shopping areas, hotels, and a bus coach and RER B station within Charles de Gaulle Airport. The complex includes the head office of Air France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GEMO_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-GEMO-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Continental_Square" title="Continental Square">Continental Square</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hilton_Hotels" title="Hilton Hotels">Hilton</a> Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and le Dôme building. Le Dôme includes the head office of Air France Consulting, an Air France subsidiary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Continental Square has the head office of <a href="/wiki/XL_Airways_France" title="XL Airways France">XL Airways France</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> the head office of Air France subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Servair" title="Servair">Servair</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and the Air France Vaccinations Centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CDGVAL">CDGVAL</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: CDGVAL">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A free automatic shuttle rail service at Charles de Gaulle Airport, consisting of two lines (<a href="/wiki/CDGVAL" title="CDGVAL">CDGVAL</a> and LISA), is based on the <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A9hicule_Automatique_L%C3%A9ger" title="Véhicule Automatique Léger">VAL</a> operational system. The shuttle train connects both railway stations for Terminals 1/3 and Terminal 2 in 8 minutes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="RER">RER</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: RER">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Charles de Gaulle airport is connected to central Paris by the <a href="/wiki/RER_B" title="RER B">RER B</a> Regional-Express services (€10 one-way as of 2016<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>). During off-peak hours and weekends, there are two types of services:</p>
<ol>
<li>4 trains per hour to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint-R%C3%A9my-l%C3%A8s-Chevreuse_(Paris_RER)" title="Saint-Rémy-lès-Chevreuse (Paris RER)">Saint-Rémy-lès-Chevreuse</a> calling at all intermediate stations to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cit%C3%A9_Universitaire_(Paris_RER)" title="Cité Universitaire (Paris RER)">Cité Universitaire</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Bourg-la-Reine" title="Bourg-la-Reine">Bourg-la-Reine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Croix_de_Berny_(Paris_RER)" title="La Croix de Berny (Paris RER)">La Croix de Berny</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antony_(Paris_RER)" title="Antony (Paris RER)">Antony</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Massy%E2%80%93Palaiseau_(Paris_RER)" title="Massy–Palaiseau (Paris RER)">Massy–Palaiseau</a> and then all stations to Saint-Rémy-lès-Chevreuse; and</li>
<li>4 trains per hour to Massy–Palaiseau (on the Saint-Rémy line), non-stop express until <a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Gare du Nord</a> and then all stations to Massy–Palaiseau.</li>
</ol>
<p>The express RER B only call at the railway stations of Terminal 1 (also for Terminal 3) and Terminal 2 before Gare du Nord. Journey time is 30–35 minutes. The stopping RER B take about 35–40 minutes and is sometimes overtaken by the express RER B trains.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_1_(Paris_RER)" title="Aéroport Charles de Gaulle 1 (Paris RER)">Aéroport Charles de Gaulle 1</a>, is located inside Roissypôle (an area with hotels and company offices) next to Terminal 3 and is the preferred way to access Terminals 1 and 3;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_2_TGV" title="Aéroport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV">Aéroport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV</a>, is located in the middle of Terminals 2C and 2E or Terminals 2D and 2F.</li>
</ul>
<p>RER B is jointly operated by <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a> and <a href="/wiki/RATP_Group" title="RATP Group">RATP</a> (Transport for Paris), but the Regional-Express used to suffer from slowness and overcrowding. For these reasons, French authorities have started two projects: <a href="/wiki/CDG_Express" title="CDG Express">CDG Express</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> which is supposed to link Charles de Gaulle Airport to Paris <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gare_de_l%27Est" title="Gare de l'Est">Gare de l'Est</a> railway station (next to Gare du Nord) from 2023 with trains specifically designed for air travellers; RER B Nord Plus,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> which modernised and streamlined RER B rail traffic and network north of Gare du Nord from 2008 to 2013 then renovated the trains from 2010 to 2015.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="TGV">TGV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: TGV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Terminal 2 includes a <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_Charles_de_Gaulle_2_TGV" title="Aéroport Charles de Gaulle 2 TGV">TGV station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/LGV_Interconnexion_Est" title="LGV Interconnexion Est">LGV Interconnexion Est</a> high-speed line. SNCF operates direct TGV services to several French stations from CDG, including <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Lille_Europe" title="Gare de Lille Europe">Lille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Strasbourg" title="Gare de Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dijon" title="Dijon">Dijon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Lyon-Part-Dieu" title="Gare de Lyon-Part-Dieu">Lyon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gare_de_Marseille_Saint-Charles" title="Gare de Marseille Saint-Charles">Marseille</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gare_de_Montpellier_Saint-Roch" title="Gare de Montpellier Saint-Roch">Montpellier</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gare_de_Toulouse_Matabiau" title="Gare de Toulouse Matabiau">Toulouse</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gare_de_Bordeaux_Saint-Jean" title="Gare de Bordeaux Saint-Jean">Bordeaux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Nantes" title="Gare de Nantes">Nantes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Poitiers" title="Gare de Poitiers">Poitiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Rennes" title="Gare de Rennes">Rennes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Toulon" title="Gare de Toulon">Toulon</a>, as well as services to <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Brussels</a> in Belgium.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Roissybus, operated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%A9gie_Autonome_des_Transports_Parisiens" title="Régie Autonome des Transports Parisiens">RATP</a> (Transport for Paris), departs from Terminals 1 and 2 and runs non-stop to <a href="/wiki/Palais_Garnier" title="Palais Garnier">Palais Garnier</a>.</li>
<li>"<i>Le Bus Direct</i>" operates to several destinations: line 2 to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Place_de_l%27Etoile" title="Place de l'Etoile">Place de l'Etoile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porte_Maillot_(Paris_M%C3%A9tro)" title="Porte Maillot (Paris Métro)">Porte Maillot</a> <a href="/wiki/Trocad%C3%A9ro" title="Trocadéro">Trocadéro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eiffel_Tower" title="Eiffel Tower">Eiffel Tower</a>, line 3 to <a href="/wiki/Orly_Airport" title="Orly Airport">Paris Orly</a> (airport south of Paris), line 4 to <a href="/wiki/Gare_Montparnasse" title="Gare Montparnasse">Gare Montparnasse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paris-Gare_de_Lyon" title="Paris-Gare de Lyon">Gare de Lyon</a> railway stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>RATP buses 350 and 351 depart from the coach station in Roissypôle (next to Terminal 1's RER railway station).</li>
<li>Bus "Magical Shuttle" departs from all three terminals for <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Paris" title="Disneyland Paris">Disneyland Paris</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>After the last RER B service at 23:50, the <a href="/wiki/Noctilien" title="Noctilien">Noctilien</a> (Night Lines) N143 and N140 depart every 30 minutes and hour respectively from Terminal 1 Door D12, Terminal 2F Door 2 and Roissypôle coach station. Both bus lines run to Paris <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Paris-Est" title="Gare de Paris-Est">Gare de l'Est</a> railway station.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ouibus">Ouibus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ouibus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 17 December 2012, <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a>'s national and international coach network, <a href="/wiki/OUIBUS" title="OUIBUS">OUIBUS</a>, serves Charles de Gaulle Airport, by terminal 3, station CDG 1.</p>
<ul>
<li>London – Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport – Lyon</li>
<li>Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport – Lyon</li>
<li>Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport – Lille</li>
<li>Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport – Brussels</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car">Car</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Car">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Charles de Gaulle Airport is directly connected to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autoroute_A1_(France)" title="Autoroute A1 (France)">Autoroute A1</a> which connects Paris and Lille.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxis_and_Transfers">Taxis and Transfers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Taxis and Transfers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The ride by taxi from CDG airport to city centre is 45 minutes and from €50 to €65, depending on the type of service/car required.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_airports">Alternative airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Alternative airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The two other airports serving Paris are <a href="/wiki/Orly_Airport" title="Orly Airport">Orly Airport</a> (south of Paris, the other major airport in Paris) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Le_Bourget_Airport" title="Le Bourget Airport">Le Bourget Airport</a> (for <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Business_jet" title="Business jet">private jets</a>).</p>
<p>Some <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost airlines</a> also advertise <a href="/wiki/Beauvais%E2%80%93Till%C3%A9_Airport" title="Beauvais–Tillé Airport">Beauvais–Tillé Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2lons_Vatry_Airport" title="Châlons Vatry Airport">Châlons Vatry Airport</a>, respectively 85 km and 165 km from Paris proper, as serving "Paris" with <i>Paris–Beauvais</i> and <i>Paris–Vatry</i>. Beauvais airport has no railway connections, but there is a shuttle bus to central Paris a few times daily.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>On 6 January 1993, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cityline_Flight_5634" title="Lufthansa Cityline Flight 5634">Lufthansa Flight 5634</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">Bremen</a> to Paris, which was carried out under the <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_CityLine" title="Lufthansa CityLine">Lufthansa CityLine</a> brand using a Contact Air <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Dash_8" title="Bombardier Dash 8">Dash 8–300</a> (<a href="/wiki/Aircraft_registration" title="Aircraft registration">registered</a> D-BEAT), hit the ground 1,800 metres (5,900 ft) short of the runway of Charles de Gaulle Airport, resulting in the death of four out of the 23 passengers on board. The four crew members survived. The accident occurred after the pilot had to abort the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aviation)" title="Final approach (aviation)">final approach</a> to the airport because the runway had been closed: the aircraft immediately ahead, a <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a>, had suffered a blown tire upon landing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>On 25 May 2000, a freight-carrying <a href="/wiki/Short_360" title="Short 360">Short SH36</a> (operated as Streamline flight 200), departing to Luton, England, collided on the runway with departing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_Liberte" title="Air Liberte">Air Liberte</a> flight 8807, an MD-83 jet. The first officer of the SH36 was killed when the wing tip of the MD-83 tore through his side of the flight deck. The captain was slightly injured and all others aboard survived.</li>
<li>On 25 July 2000, a <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_4590" title="Air France Flight 4590">Air France Flight 4590</a> from Charles de Gaulle to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> in New York, crashed into Les Relais Bleus Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Gonesse" title="Gonesse">Gonesse</a>, killing everyone on the aircraft and four people on the ground. Investigations concluded that a tire burst on take-off due to metal left on the runway from a previously departing aircraft, leading to a ruptured fuel tank and resulting in engine failure and other damage. Concorde was conducting a charter flight for a German tour company.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theft">Theft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Theft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>In December 2006, 20 baggage handlers were found guilty of theft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_Property_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-French_Property-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2007, 19 baggage handlers were found guilty of theft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_Property_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-French_Property-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>In September 2008, 12 baggage handlers were arrested on suspicion of stealing goods from luggages worth 450,000 euros.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>In February 2011, 20 baggage handlers were arrested on suspicion of stealing from the luggage of passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li>In November 2012, 11 baggage handlers and 2 maintenance workers were arrested for stealing valuable items from luggage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Animals">Animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Animals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The grassy lands on which the airport is located are notorious for rabbits and <a href="/wiki/Hare" title="Hare">hares</a>, which can be seen by passengers at certain times of the day. The airport organises periodic hunts and captures to keep the population to manageable levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
